parameter, uniquely characterized by values of density parameters (&#937;<sub>M</sub> for <a href="/wiki/Matter" title="Matter">matter</a> and &#937;<sub>&#923;</sub> for <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">dark energy</a>). A "closed universe" with &#937;<sub>M</sub> &gt; 1 and &#937;<sub>&#923;</sub> = 0 comes to an end in a <a href="/wiki/Big_Crunch" title="Big Crunch">Big Crunch</a> and is considerably younger than its Hubble age. An "open universe" with &#937;<sub>M</sub> &#8804; 1 and &#937;<sub>&#923;</sub> = 0 expands forever and has an age that is closer to its Hubble age. For the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accelerating_universe" title="Accelerating universe">accelerating universe</a> with nonzero &#937;<sub>&#923;</sub> that we inhabit, the age of the universe is coincidentally very close to the Hubble age.</div></div></div>\n<p>The value of the Hubble parameter changes over time, either increasing or decreasing depending on the value of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Deceleration_parameter" title="Deceleration parameter">deceleration parameter</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle q}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>q</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle q}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="q" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/06809d64fa7c817ffc7e323f85997f783dbdf71d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.07ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>, which is defined by\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle q=-\\left(1+{\\frac {\\dot {H}}{H^{2}}}\\right).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>q</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mo>&#729;<!-- &#729; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle q=-\\left(1+{\\frac {\\dot {H}}{H^{2}}}\\right).}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="q=-\\left(1+{\\frac  {{\\dot  H}}{H^{2}}}\\right)." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ddaa2e820b7e67291868f468e5adb91f9f529439" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:19.075ex; height:7.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>In a universe with a deceleration parameter equal to zero, it follows that <i>H</i> = 1/<i>t</i>, where <i>t</i> is the time since the Big Bang. A non-zero, time-dependent value of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle q}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>q</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle q}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="q" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/06809d64fa7c817ffc7e323f85997f783dbdf71d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.07ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> simply requires <a href="/wiki/Integral" title="Integral">integration</a> of the Friedmann equations backwards from the present time to the time when the <a href="/wiki/Particle_horizon" title="Particle horizon">comoving horizon</a> size was zero.\n</p><p>It was long thought that <i>q</i> was positive, indicating that the expansion is slowing down due to gravitational attraction. This would imply an age of the universe less than 1/<i>H</i> (which is about 14 billion years). For instance, a value for <i>q</i> of 1/2 (once favoured by most theorists) would give the age of the universe as 2/(3<i>H</i>). The discovery in 1998 that <i>q</i> is apparently negative means that the universe could actually be older than 1/<i>H</i>. However, estimates of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_the_universe" title="Age of the universe">age of the universe</a> are very close to 1/<i>H</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Olbers.27_paradox"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Olbers\'_paradox">Olbers\' paradox</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Olbers\' paradox">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Olbers%27_paradox" title="Olbers\' paradox">Olbers\' paradox</a></div>\n<p>The expansion of space summarized by the Big Bang interpretation of Hubble\'s law is relevant to the old conundrum known as <a href="/wiki/Olbers%27_paradox" title="Olbers\' paradox">Olbers\' paradox</a>: If the universe were <a href="/wiki/Infinity" title="Infinity">infinite</a> in size, <a href="/wiki/Static_universe" title="Static universe">static</a>, and filled with a uniform distribution of <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">stars</a>, then every line of sight in the sky would end on a star, and the sky would be as <a href="/wiki/Brightness" title="Brightness">bright</a> as the surface of a star. However, the night sky is largely dark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chase_etal_2004_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chase_etal_2004-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asimov1974_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asimov1974-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the 17th&#160;century, astronomers and other thinkers have proposed many possible ways to resolve this paradox, but the currently accepted resolution depends in part on the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">Big Bang</a> theory, and in part on the Hubble expansion: In a universe that exists for a finite amount of time, only the light of a finite number of stars has had enough time to reach us, and the paradox is resolved. Additionally, in an expanding universe, distant objects <a href="/wiki/Recessional_velocity" title="Recessional velocity">recede</a> from us, which causes the light emanated from them to be <a href="/wiki/Redshift" title="Redshift">redshifted</a> and diminished in brightness by the time we see it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chase_etal_2004_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chase_etal_2004-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asimov1974_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Asimov1974-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dimensionless_Hubble_parameter">Dimensionless Hubble parameter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Dimensionless Hubble parameter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Instead of working with Hubble\'s constant, a common practice is to introduce the <b>dimensionless Hubble parameter</b>, usually denoted by <i>h</i>, and to write the Hubble\'s parameter <i>H</i><sub>0</sub> as <i>h</i>&#160;&#215;&#160;100&#160;km&#160;<a href="/wiki/Second" title="Second">s</a><sup>&#8722;1</sup>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Parsec" title="Parsec">Mpc</a><sup>&#8722;1</sup>, all the relative uncertainty of the true value of <i>H</i><sub>0</sub> being then relegated to <i>h</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Occasionally a reference value different to 100 may be chosen, in which case a subscript is presented after <i>h</i> to avoid confusion; e.g. h<sub>70</sub> denotes <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle H_{0}=70\\,h_{70}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>70</mn>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<msub>\n<mi>h</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>70</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle H_{0}=70\\,h_{70}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle H_{0}=70\\,h_{70}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a9606e88a6301f69e96d948deb43761d6a27a7f2" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.011ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> km&#160;s<sup>&#8722;1</sup>&#160;Mpc<sup>&#8722;1</sup>, which implies <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle h_{70}=h/0.7}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>h</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>70</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>h</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mn>0.7</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle h_{70}=h/0.7}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle h_{70}=h/0.7}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3ef32be16fa72d483ee8070e05f793ad04e2e1f0" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.787ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.\n</p><p>This should not be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Dimensionless_physical_constant" title="Dimensionless physical constant">dimensionless value</a> of Hubble\'s constant, usually expressed in terms of <a href="/wiki/Planck_units" title="Planck units">Planck units</a>, with current  of <i>H</i><sub>0</sub>&#215;<a href="/wiki/Planck_time" title="Planck time"><i>t</i><sub>P</sub></a>&#160;=&#160;1.18&#160;&#215;&#160;10<sup>&#8722;61</sup>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="A citation might let the reader know which value of the Hubble Constant is being used. Alternatively and/or in addition, the reader should be told in our article text which value is being used. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Determining_the_Hubble_constant">Determining the Hubble constant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Determining the Hubble constant">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Recent_Hubble%27s_Constant_Values.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="265" decoding="async" height="357" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Recent_Hubble%27s_Constant_Values.png/220px-Recent_Hubble%27s_Constant_Values.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/Recent_Hubble%27s_Constant_Values.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Recent_Hubble%27s_Constant_Values.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Value of the Hubble Constant including measurement uncertainty for recent surveys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planck_overview_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-planck_overview-38">[38]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The value of the Hubble constant is estimated by measuring the <a href="/wiki/Redshift" title="Redshift">redshift</a> of distant galaxies and then <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_distance_ladder" title="Cosmic distance ladder">determining the distances to the same galaxies</a> (by some other method than Hubble\'s law). Uncertainties in the physical assumptions used to determine these distances have caused varying estimates of the Hubble constant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20170220_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20170220-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The observations of astronomer <a href="/wiki/Walter_Baade" title="Walter Baade">Walter Baade</a> led him to define distinct "<a href="/wiki/Stellar_population" title="Stellar population">populations</a>" for stars (Population I and Population II). The same observations led him to discover that there are two types of <a href="/wiki/Cepheid_variable" title="Cepheid variable">Cepheid variable</a> stars. Using this discovery he recalculated the size of the known universe, doubling the previous calculation made by <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Hubble" title="Edwin Hubble">Hubble</a> in 1929.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> He announced this finding to considerable astonishment at the 1952 meeting of the <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">International Astronomical Union</a> in Rome.\n</p><p>In October 2018, scientists presented a new third way (two earlier methods, one based on <a href="/wiki/Redshift" title="Redshift">redshifts</a> and another on the <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_distance_ladder" title="Cosmic distance ladder">cosmic distance ladder</a>, gave results that do not agree), using information from <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_wave" title="Gravitational wave">gravitational wave</a> events (especially those involving the <a href="/wiki/Neutron_star_merger" title="Neutron star merger">merger of neutron stars</a>, like <a href="/wiki/GW170817" title="GW170817">GW170817</a>), of determining the Hubble Constant, essential in establishing the rate of <a href="/wiki/Expansion_of_the_universe" title="Expansion of the universe">expansion of the universe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PHYS-20181022_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-PHYS-20181022-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAT-20181017_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-NAT-20181017-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earlier_measurement_and_discussion_approaches">Earlier measurement and discussion approaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Earlier measurement and discussion approaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For most of the second half of the 20th century the value of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle H_{0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle H_{0}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="H_{0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/43910602a221b7a4c373791f94793e3008622070" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.985ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> was estimated to be between 50 and <span class="nowrap">90 (km/s)/Mpc</span>.\n</p><p>The value of the Hubble constant was the topic of a long and rather bitter controversy between <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_de_Vaucouleurs" title="G&#233;rard de Vaucouleurs">G&#233;rard de Vaucouleurs</a>, who claimed the value was around 100, and <a href="/wiki/Allan_Sandage" title="Allan Sandage">Allan Sandage</a>, who claimed the value was near 50.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overbye_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Overbye-51">[51]</a></sup> In 1996, a debate moderated by <a href="/wiki/John_N._Bahcall" title="John N. Bahcall">John Bahcall</a> between <a href="/wiki/Sidney_van_den_Bergh" title="Sidney van den Bergh">Sidney van den Bergh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Andreas_Tammann" title="Gustav Andreas Tammann">Gustav Tammann</a> was held in similar fashion to the earlier <a href="/wiki/Great_Debate_(astronomy)" title="Great Debate (astronomy)">Shapley-Curtis debate</a> over these two competing values.\n</p><p>This previously wide variance in estimates was partially resolved with the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Lambda-CDM_model" title="Lambda-CDM model">&#923;CDM model</a> of the universe in the late 1990s. With the &#923;CDM model observations of high-redshift clusters at X-ray and microwave wavelengths using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunyaev%E2%80%93Zel%27dovich_effect" title="Sunyaev&#8211;Zel\'dovich effect">Sunyaev&#8211;Zel\'dovich effect</a>, measurements of anisotropies in the <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background" title="Cosmic microwave background">cosmic microwave background</a> radiation, and optical surveys all gave a value of around 70 for the constant.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>More recent measurements from the <a href="/wiki/Planck_(spacecraft)" title="Planck (spacecraft)">Planck mission</a> indicate a lower value of around 67;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planck_overview_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-planck_overview-38">[38]</a></sup> although, even more recently, in February 2018, a higher value of 73 has been determined using an improved procedure involving the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20180222_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20180222-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>See table of measurements above for many recent and older measurements.</i>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acceleration_of_the_expansion">Acceleration of the expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Acceleration of the expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accelerating_universe" title="Accelerating universe">Accelerating universe</a></div>\n<p>A value for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle q}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>q</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle q}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="q" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/06809d64fa7c817ffc7e323f85997f783dbdf71d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.07ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> measured from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_candle" title="Standard candle">standard candle</a> observations of <a href="/wiki/Type_Ia_supernova" title="Type Ia supernova">Type Ia supernovae</a>, which was determined in 1998 to be negative, surprised many astronomers with the implication that the expansion of the universe is currently "accelerating"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> (although the Hubble factor is still decreasing with time, as mentioned above in the <a href="/wiki/Hubble%27s_law#Interpretation" title="Hubble\'s law">Interpretation</a> section; see the articles on <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">dark energy</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%CE%9BCDM_model" title="&#923;CDM model">&#923;CDM model</a>).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Derivation_of_the_Hubble_parameter">Derivation of the Hubble parameter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Derivation of the Hubble parameter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Start with the <a href="/wiki/Friedmann_equations" title="Friedmann equations">Friedmann equation</a>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle H^{2}\\equiv \\left({\\frac <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho _{m_{0}}}" width:11.953ex; height:6.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where the subscript nought refers to the values today, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle a_{0}=1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle a_{0}=1}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="a_{0}=1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e3873789cb6451e25f63b4d11572ac5c69d7873b" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.545ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>. Substituting all of this into the Friedmann equation at the start of this section and replacing <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle a}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle a=1/(1+z)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle a=1/(1+z)}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="a=1/(1+z)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0b7a85819fad51e37f1513c036df0c6aade4d1e1" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.553ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> gives\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}(1+z)^{3}+\\Omega _{k}(1+z)^{2}+\\Omega _{\\Lambda }\\right).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>m</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>k</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#923;<!-- &#923; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}(1+z)^{3}+\\Omega _{k}(1+z)^{2}+\\Omega _{\\Lambda }\\right).}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}(1+z)^{3}+\\Omega _{k}(1+z)^{2}+\\Omega _{\\Lambda }\\right).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/137b7a46468546b46444dc0c1210129f03760f82" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:46.623ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Matter-_and_dark_energy-dominated_universe">Matter- and dark energy-dominated universe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Matter- and dark energy-dominated universe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>If the universe is both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matter-dominated_era" title="Matter-dominated era">matter-dominated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">dark energy</a>-dominated, then the above equation for the Hubble parameter will also be a function of the <a href="/wiki/Equation_of_state_(cosmology)" title="Equation of state (cosmology)">equation of state of dark energy</a>. So now:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho =\\rho _{m}(a)+\\rho _{de}(a),}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>m</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\rho =\\rho _{m}(a)+\\rho _{de}(a),}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\rho =\\rho _{m}(a)+\\rho _{{de}}(a)," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e9b7e988fbf94cd08610cfca88c88ce2453d6994" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:19.803ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\rho _{{de}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/85d101ac290db841549ea7d3c2ef9384841cd861" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.06ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is the mass density of the dark energy. By definition, an equation of state in cosmology is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle P=w\\rho c^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>P</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle P=w\\rho c^{2}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="P=w\\rho c^{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/79d4d9bb42bba8a80d5e01e467bb6dbb6d69566a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.771ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span>, and if this is substituted into the fluid equation, which describes how the mass density of the universe evolves with time, then\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\dot {\\rho }}+3{\\frac {\\dot {a}}{a}}\\left(\\rho +{\\frac {P}{c^{2}}}\\right)=0;}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mo>&#729;<!-- &#729; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo>&#729;<!-- &#729; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>P</mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n<mo>;</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\dot {\\rho }}+3{\\frac {\\dot {a}}{a}}\\left(\\rho +{\\frac {P}{c^{2}}}\\right)=0;}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\dot  {\\rho }}+3{\\frac  {{\\dot  {a}}}{a}}\\left(\\rho +{\\frac  {P}{c^{2}}}\\right)=0;" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9146107d8b7136759cc40ca3279885d5f7953431" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:23.1ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd>\n<dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {d\\rho }{\\rho }}=-3{\\frac {da}{a}}(1+w).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\frac {d\\rho }{\\rho }}=-3{\\frac {da}{a}}(1+w).}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {d\\rho }{\\rho }}=-3{\\frac {da}{a}}(1+w).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/96cb9aeca43b3d11373c63505bf2c6f87e915186" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:20.728ex; height:5.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>If <i>w</i> is constant, then\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\ln {\\rho }=-3(1+w)\\ln {a};}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>ln</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mi>ln</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo>;</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\ln {\\rho }=-3(1+w)\\ln {a};}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\ln {\\rho }=-3(1+w)\\ln {a};}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/451d0ddb9e71f10472c233137b70f55aee9e3af7" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:21.664ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>implying:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho =a^{-3(1+w)}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\rho =a^{-3(1+w)}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\rho =a^{-3(1+w)}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e9c07b156f1101ae7a03b9177d1d28d80b3d9f61" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.066ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Therefore, for dark energy with a constant equation of state <i>w</i>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de}(a)=\\rho _{de0}a^{-3(1+w)}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<msup>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de}(a)=\\rho _{de0}a^{-3(1+w)}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de}(a)=\\rho _{de0}a^{-3(1+w)}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a38cdc5702187699d6d3d985b079ec823da8562a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:21.199ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span>. If this is substituted into the Friedman equation in a similar way as before, but this time set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle k=0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>k</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle k=0}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="k=0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6307c8a99dad7d0bcb712352ae0a748bd99a038b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.472ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, which assumes a spatially flat universe, then (see <a href="/wiki/Shape_of_the_universe" title="Shape of the universe">Shape of the universe</a>)\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}(1+z)^{3}+\\Omega _{de}(1+z)^{3(1+w)}\\right).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>m</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}(1+z)^{3}+\\Omega _{de}(1+z)^{3(1+w)}\\right).}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}(1+z)^{3}+\\Omega _{de}(1+z)^{3(1+w)}\\right).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dca5516af863e458b67a8f228f1871720fa5a0dc" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:46.703ex; height:4.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>If the dark energy derives from a cosmological constant such as that introduced by Einstein, it can be shown that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle w=-1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle w=-1}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="w=-1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e0dc6e8ffa1ebcf4456ba3b4e1c79f0ca92fba76" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:7.733ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>. The equation then reduces to the last equation in the matter-dominated universe section, with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Omega _{k}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>k</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Omega _{k}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\Omega_k " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b18029871270775ecb905d24b7fc1a0016930965" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.767ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> set to zero. In that case the initial dark energy density <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de0}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\rho_{de0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/593c1f80df14f12eaa04f32a0b804b5dac49195b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.882ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is given by<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de0}={\\frac {\\Lambda c^{2}}{8\\pi G}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#923;<!-- &#923; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mn>8</mn>\n<mi>&#960;<!-- &#960; --></mi>\n<mi>G</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de0}={\\frac {\\Lambda c^{2}}{8\\pi G}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\rho_{de0} =  \\frac{\\Lambda c^2}{8 \\pi G} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6df1172f26645e6bedce0c0d42953b7ff1c842e3" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:12.138ex; height:5.843ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Omega _{de}=\\Omega _{\\Lambda }.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>d</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#923;<!-- &#923; width:10.332ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>If dark energy does not have a constant equation-of-state w, then\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho _{de}(a)=\\rho _{de0}e^{-3\\int {\\frac {da}{a}}\\left(1+w(a)\\right)},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961; width:4.703ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> must be parametrized, for example if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle w(a)=w_{0}+w_{a}(1-a)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle w(a)=w_{0}+w_{a}(1-a)}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="w(a)=w_{0}+w_{a}(1-a)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e1bf8900fe735859f3209a6c032707ea6fb16c5" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:23.168ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, giving\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}a^{-3}+\\Omega _{de}a^{-3\\left(1+w_{0}+w_{a}\\right)}e^{-3w_{a}(1-a)}\\right).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>m</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<msup>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#937;<!-- &#937; --></mo>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<msub>\n<mi>w</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}a^{-3}+\\Omega _{de}a^{-3\\left(1+w_{0}+w_{a}\\right)}e^{-3w_{a}(1-a)}\\right).}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle H^{2}(z)=H_{0}^{2}\\left(\\Omega _{m}a^{-3}+\\Omega _{de}a^{-3\\left(1+w_{0}+w_{a}\\right)}e^{-3w_{a}(1-a)}\\right).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1fa3b2c576aae1369f5ca90b1d87467edc432db9" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:51.789ex; height:4.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Other ingredients have been formulated recently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Units_derived_from_the_Hubble_constant">Units derived from the Hubble constant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Units derived from the Hubble constant">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Hubble time">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Hubble constant <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle H_{0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle H_{0}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="H_{0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/43910602a221b7a4c373791f94793e3008622070" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.985ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> has units of inverse time; the <b>Hubble time</b> <i>t<sub>H</sub></i> is simply defined as the inverse of the Hubble constant,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> i.e.\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle t_{H}\\equiv {\\frac {1}{H_{0}}}={\\frac {1}{67.8{\\textrm {(km/s)/Mpc}}}}=4.55\\cdot 10^{17}{\\textrm {s}}=14.4{\\text{ billion years}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>H</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8801;<!-- &#8801; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<msub>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mn>67.8</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>(km/s)/Mpc</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>4.55</mn>\n<mo>&#8901;<!-- &#8901; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mn>10</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>17</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>s</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>14.4</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>&#160;billion years</mtext>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle t_{H}\\equiv {\\frac {1}{H_{0}}}={\\frac {1}{67.8{\\textrm {(km/s)/Mpc}}}}=4.55\\cdot 10^{17}{\\textrm {s}}=14.4{\\text{ billion years}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle t_{H}\\equiv {\\frac {1}{H_{0}}}={\\frac {1}{67.8{\\textrm {(km/s)/Mpc}}}}=4.55\\cdot 10^{17}{\\textrm {s}}=14.4{\\text{ billion years}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e8b5aaa1a0f5cdd006057d96ca180bbb9053677f" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:64.845ex; height:6.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>This is slightly different from the age of the universe which is approximately 13.8 billion years. The Hubble time is the age it would have had if the expansion had been linear, and it is different from the real age of the universe because the expansion is not linear; they are related by a dimensionless factor which depends on the mass-energy content of the universe, which is around 0.96 in the standard <a href="/wiki/Lambda-CDM_model" title="Lambda-CDM model">Lambda-CDM model</a>.\n</p><p>We currently appear to be approaching a period where the expansion of the universe is exponential due to the increasing dominance of <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_energy" title="Vacuum energy">vacuum energy</a>. In this regime, the Hubble parameter is constant, and the universe grows by a factor <a href="/wiki/E_(mathematical_constant)" title="E (mathematical constant)"><i>e</i></a> each Hubble time:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle H\\equiv {\\frac {\\dot {a}}{a}}={\\textrm {constant}}\\quad \\Longrightarrow \\quad a\\propto e^{Ht}=e^{\\frac {t}{t_{H}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mo>&#8801;<!-- &#8801; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo>&#729;<!-- &#729; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>constant</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mspace width="1em"></mspace>\n<mo stretchy="false">&#10233;<!-- &#10233; --></mo>\n<mspace width="1em"></mspace>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo>&#8733;<!-- &#8733; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>H</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle H\\equiv {\\frac {\\dot {a}}{a}}={\\textrm {constant}}\\quad \\Longrightarrow \\quad a\\propto e^{Ht}=e^{\\frac {t}{t_{H}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle H\\equiv {\\frac {\\dot {a}}{a}}={\\textrm {constant}}\\quad \\Longrightarrow \\quad a\\propto e^{Ht}=e^{\\frac {t}{t_{H}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d99e523759010972346c125777b6e84e739881f4" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:43.483ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Over long periods of time, the dynamics are complicated by <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">dark energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inflation_(cosmology)" title="Inflation (cosmology)">inflation</a>, etc., as explained above.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hubble_length">Hubble length</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Hubble length">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Hubble length or Hubble distance is a unit of distance in cosmology, defined as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/509bf59fe1c2c452277a681c0bf5a11584f77574" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:5.443ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span> &#8212; the speed of light multiplied by the Hubble time. It is equivalent to 4,550 million parsecs or 14.4 billion light years. (The numerical value of the Hubble length in light years is, by definition, equal to that of the Hubble time in years.) The Hubble distance would be the distance between the Earth and the galaxies which are <i>currently</i> receding from us at the speed of light, as can be seen by substituting <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle D=cH_{0}^{-1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>D</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle D=cH_{0}^{-1}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle D=cH_{0}^{-1}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ad92d7fe31933d41f909359ce2e5e996bb5078e2" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:10.466ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span> into the equation for Hubble\'s law, <span class="nowrap"><i>v</i> = <i>H</i><sub>0</sub><i>D</i></span>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hubble_volume">Hubble volume</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Hubble volume">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hubble_volume" title="Hubble volume">Hubble volume</a></div>\n<p>The Hubble volume is sometimes defined as a volume of the universe with a <a href="/wiki/Comoving_and_proper_distances" title="Comoving and proper distances">comoving</a> size of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a041fa30dc106661de9364834641e7783e735673" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:6.09ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span> The exact definition varies: it is sometimes defined as the volume of a sphere with radius <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/088cba4ac16bc846cb8946843f3d526a4f01432f" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:6.09ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span> or alternatively, a cube of side <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>c</mi>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>H</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle cH_{0}^{-1}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a041fa30dc106661de9364834641e7783e735673" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:6.09ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span> Some cosmologists even use the term Hubble volume to refer to the volume of the <a href="/wiki/Observable_universe" title="Observable universe">observable universe</a>, although this has a radius approximately three times larger.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hubble%27s_law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
